  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_054f9154-597c-4923-8d36-172abb2ea125'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {

              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});

<div id="review_706436808" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/706436808" />
    <a title="Simon Taylor" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23284117-simon-taylor"><img alt="Simon Taylor" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442951658p2/23284117.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/706436808?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simon Taylor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simon Taylor" href="/user/show/23284117-simon-taylor">Simon Taylor</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer706436808" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8747683085329671609">The first case for Detective Superintendent Roy Grace was a relatively unique thriller in the way it was presented. The basic storyline is thus: groom goes on stag night, groom buried in coffin as stag night joke, stags killed in car accident, hunt for missing groom.<br/><br/>From the outset, we are told that his best man knows where he is but is keeping silent, effectively allowing him to die. The book follows the story through the victim, the would-be murderer and the detective. Itâs not a whodunnit, or</span>
  <span id="freeText8747683085329671609" style="display:none">The first case for Detective Superintendent Roy Grace was a relatively unique thriller in the way it was presented. The basic storyline is thus: groom goes on stag night, groom buried in coffin as stag night joke, stags killed in car accident, hunt for missing groom.<br /><br />From the outset, we are told that his best man knows where he is but is keeping silent, effectively allowing him to die. The book follows the story through the victim, the would-be murderer and the detective. Itâs not a whodunnit, or even a howdunnit, more of a what-are-they-going-to-do-now-since-theyâve-dunnit.<br /><br />Letâs start with the victim. Michael Harrison may or may not survive his coffin ordeal, and unlike many whodunnits that start with a body, we suffer with the victim through what could be his final days. The scenes are well written and very claustrophobic, and the reader feels Michaelâs panic, hope and disappointments.<br /><br />The villains of the piece are a little underdeveloped. Although some thought has gone into each character, theyâre quite one-dimensional and could have been more rounded.<br /><br />And Detective Superintendent Grace, the star of the show and of this new series? A down-to-earth and likeable character who has a dry sense of humour and strong sense of conviction. Heâs achieved moderate success but has his frustrations. The disappearance of his wife ten years ago looks set to be a theme which will continue through the series, and one particularly pertinent to this case, even if dealt with a little inconsistently. He keeps her toothbrush and dressing gown in situ in case she returns, but also goes on two dates in the course of the book. Is this the realisation of his own inner conflict, or just poor writing?<br /><br />As a standalone book, Grace would have been forgettable. But for a long-running series, his character could be slow-burner weâre going to keep learning more about, and itâs a journey Iâm happy to take with him.<br /><br />Set in Brighton, there are a number of welcome reminders that itâs a UK series with lots of cultural references. As police procedurals go, James has done his homework and provides detailed, interesting background to the inner workings of Brightonâs police force. Having said that, it seems American in tone and I wasnât surprised to learn subsequently that James has written screenplays in the US.<br /><br />I was also slightly annoyed by silly mistakes â quotation marks opening again in the middle of speech, at one point not closing, elsewhere missing out an apostrophe. Basic errors and editor should have spotted. Elsewhere, swearing was used too gratuitously and the sex scenes were perhaps more graphic than necessary.<br /><br />The plot moves quickly and the chapters are short, giving great readability. Some of the twists are far fetched, and Grace appears thick as a brick. Although the reader has the benefit of knowing whatâs going on, Grace bumbles along wondering, âI have 1 and 1, I wonder what they equal?â<br /><br />Very obvious conclusions are not made where they should have been. Easy leads arenât picked up on. And instead of proper police work or following up on these leads, the man seems lead by hunches. And thenâ¦<br /><br />Spoiler warning<br /><br /><br />Normally, I keep my review strictly spoiler free, but on this occasion I feel compelled to make an exception. Forgetting all else, the case starts and ends as a missing person investigation. The thrust, the purpose, is to find the missing person.<br /><br />A reasonably written book with a great ending would have been a respectable 4 out of 5. An ending in keeping with the writing, a healthy 3. But I canât go any higher than 2 on the basis of what unfolded.<br /><br />Harrison is found (though Iâm not saying whether alive or dead) in the final couple of pages. How? Grace chucks a psychic in the car, the psychic says âHeâs hereâ and hey presto!<br /><br />I accept police forces may use mediums at times, and it was reportedly used in the search for Madeline McCann. But readers of detective books want to see their stars solve mysteries by detection, not by some bloke humming over cufflinks. It robs us of an ending, itâs a complete cop out and breaks the unwritten rules of the genre. Any detective story could end that way. (âOoo, aaaahhh, uuummmm. The spirits tell me the butler did it, Poirot.â) Itâs lazy, so lazy, and cheapens the whole affair.<br /><br />For that reason, I cannot recommend Dead Simple, because if the author didnât care enough about the book to even devise and ending â why should we care either?</span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer442697067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10322806912603144669">The beginning of this book is the creepiest I have ever run across. Anxious to play a prank on their soon-to-be-married friend Michael Harrison, known for his pranks, four of his friends get him drunk and passed out, then bury him in a coffin with only a tube for air, a porn magazine and a walkie-talkie. Then they drive off and are T-boned by a concrete truck. All are killed. The tow truck driver's retarded son (or should I say mentally challenged), finds the walkie-talkie in the grass where it </span>
  <span id="freeText10322806912603144669" style="display:none">The beginning of this book is the creepiest I have ever run across. Anxious to play a prank on their soon-to-be-married friend Michael Harrison, known for his pranks, four of his friends get him drunk and passed out, then bury him in a coffin with only a tube for air, a porn magazine and a walkie-talkie. Then they drive off and are T-boned by a concrete truck. All are killed. The tow truck driver's retarded son (or should I say mentally challenged), finds the walkie-talkie in the grass where it had been thrown by the accident, talks to Michael, but then drops it and thinks he has broken the unit. Now he's afraid to tell anyone about what he found. Michael's realization that he is buried and that no one is answering his increasing frantic calls on the walkie-talkie will give you nightmares, or at least it would, if you're susceptible to that sort of thing. Forget supernatural/horror crap, realism is far more frightening. <br /><br /> Superintendent Roy Grace is charged with finding the missing man who disappeared just three days before he was to be married. Michael's friend and business partner we soon learn has it in for Michael and Ashley's Michael's intended is startled to learn that the business had considerable funds in a Cayman Islands account. Or is she? (Spoiler police, please note:These really aren't spoilers as we learn the details from several points of view early in the book.) The scenes of Michael growing increasingly frantic in his coffin are really frightening. Some interesting twists kept things moving along nicely.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10322806912603144669" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1825916055" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1825916055" />
    <a title="MadProfessah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2116192-madprofessah"><img alt="MadProfessah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1482687972p2/2116192.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1825916055?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MadProfessah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MadProfessah" href="/user/show/2116192-madprofessah">MadProfessah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11317129-dead-simple">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2116192-madprofessah?shelf=2020-read">2020-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1825916055" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8419038112360085906">This is the first book I have read by Peter James. It is a pretty straightforward entry in the British police procedural genre, with Detective Chief Superintendent Roy Grace as the main protagonist. Grace is a 39-year-old single man whose beloved wife disappeared nearly 9 years ago without a trace, but whom he has refused to have declared dead. Graceâs main sidekick is a fellow police officer, a Black bodybuilder named Glenn Branson. There are other sidekicks as well as a potential love interest</span>
  <span id="freeText8419038112360085906" style="display:none">This is the first book I have read by Peter James. It is a pretty straightforward entry in the British police procedural genre, with Detective Chief Superintendent Roy Grace as the main protagonist. Grace is a 39-year-old single man whose beloved wife disappeared nearly 9 years ago without a trace, but whom he has refused to have declared dead. Graceâs main sidekick is a fellow police officer, a Black bodybuilder named Glenn Branson. There are other sidekicks as well as a potential love interest for Grace which I presume will develop in the future.<br /><br />The key strength of DEAD SIMPLE is the thrilling premise. A group of 4 friends takes a buddy out for a âstag nightâ a week before his wedding. Michael has played pranks on each of his friends and they decide to get revenge by leaving him in a buried coffin with a walkie-talkie, a bottle of whiskey and a straw for air for a few hours. Unfortunately they get in a horrific car accident which kills them all, leaving Michael trapped in a grave where it appears no one knows he is. <br /><br />With the clock continually ticking towards a time when Michael will either die by dehydration, starvation or both, the plot becomes more complicated as Michaelâs fiancÃ© Ashley and best friend &amp; business partner Mark appear to be reacting strangely to Michaelâs disappearance. Although it begins as Bransonâs case, eventually Grace himself gets involved and there are many surprising plot twists which demonstrate why Peter James is such a bestselling author of suspense thrillers. One slight wrinkle for me is apparently Grace is a believer in the supernatural and has used (and continues to use) mediums and similar dodgy means to help him make breakthroughs in cases. I can appreciate some âgenre crossoverâ but supernatural is not my favorite blend. (I really love a good sci-fi mystery mix.)<br /><br />Overall, I was impressed with DEAD SIMPLE and am definitely interested in going on future adventures with Roy Grace as I read the subsequent books in the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8419038112360085906" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Sandy *The world could end while I was reading and I would never notice*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice"><img alt="Sandy *The world could end while I was reading and I would never notice*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509647506p2/30817744.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1001327189?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandy *The world could end while I was reading and I would never notice*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandy *The world could end while I was reading and I would never notice*" href="/user/show/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice">Sandy *The world could end while I was reading and I would never notice*</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1001327189" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9128469989234781545">Another great read from Peter James.<br/><br/>I was intrigued by the idea of putting someone into a coffin as a bucks night stunt - the thought of being that person terrified me - and then I found out that Peter James had actually done it for research into his book. Brave man!<br/><br/>While out celebrating with a group of friends a few nights before his wedding, Michael suddenly and unexpectedly finds himself enclosed in a coffin equipped only with a flashlight, a dirty magazine, a walkie-talkie, and a tiny breath</span>
  <span id="freeText9128469989234781545" style="display:none">Another great read from Peter James.<br /><br />I was intrigued by the idea of putting someone into a coffin as a bucks night stunt - the thought of being that person terrified me - and then I found out that Peter James had actually done it for research into his book. Brave man!<br /><br />While out celebrating with a group of friends a few nights before his wedding, Michael suddenly and unexpectedly finds himself enclosed in a coffin equipped only with a flashlight, a dirty magazine, a walkie-talkie, and a tiny breathing tube. It's all in good fun â payback for the grief his mates suffered due to his own penchant for tomfoolery â that is until the four are killed in a drunk driving accident just moments after leaving Michael completely alone and buried alive. <br /><br />But one of his mates never made it to the bucks party, and Detective Superintendent Grace thinks both he and the dead man's fiancee know more than they are letting on.<br /><br />I really enjoyed re-reading this book, and will continue on with the remainder of the series.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_995353788" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/995353788" />
    <a title="Mark Rubinstein" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10469395-mark-rubinstein"><img alt="Mark Rubinstein" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442454730p2/10469395.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/995353788?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mark Rubinstein" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mark Rubinstein" href="/user/show/10469395-mark-rubinstein">Mark Rubinstein</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer995353788" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4862446153709394371"><i>Dead Simple</i> is the first of Peter James's novels about Brighton-based detective Roy Grace. It has a compelling narrative arc in which a practical joke involving a coffin is central. The writing is excellent and, at times, beautiful. There are many twists and turns that keep the reader trying to maintain balance, and the novel is a perfect baseline for the others coming after it in this series. A well-deserved five stars.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer445950391" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2995381583326591632">This book was recommended to me by a stranger while I was browsing in a bookstore. It's rare when another customer out of the blue recommends you read a book without knowing anything about your tastes, so I knew I had to read this book. And that other customer was right, I loved this book and will absolutely read the next book in the series. <br/>The plot is one of the most inventive and entertaining ones that I have ever read. The story begins with a batchelor party gone horribly wrong, five friends</span>
  <span id="freeText2995381583326591632" style="display:none">This book was recommended to me by a stranger while I was browsing in a bookstore. It's rare when another customer out of the blue recommends you read a book without knowing anything about your tastes, so I knew I had to read this book. And that other customer was right, I loved this book and will absolutely read the next book in the series. <br />The plot is one of the most inventive and entertaining ones that I have ever read. The story begins with a batchelor party gone horribly wrong, five friends go out for an evening of partying with a plan to give the groom, a serial practical joker, some of his own medicine. They plan to give him a little scare by burying him alive. Tragedy strikes when his friends get into a car accident, killing 3 of them immediately, leaving the fourth in a coma, and the groom buried alive. Wow - what a begining, and the plot just keeps getting better with its many twists and turns. Highly recommended!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2995381583326591632" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=omg-so-exciting-couldnt-stop-readin">omg-so-exciting-couldnt-stop-readin</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer18118678451726420973"><br/>The book opens on the concluding hours of a drunken stag party. The young men celebrating Michael Harrisonâs incipient wedding to Ashley which is to take place in three days have known each other for years, so whenever one of the friends marries, they plot practical jokes and get blind drunk. Michael himself has been behind several particularly fiendish jokes, so his friends are looking forward to the payback they have developed for Michael. Days before, with shovels and a coffin and a breathing</span>
  <span id="freeText18118678451726420973" style="display:none"><br />The book opens on the concluding hours of a drunken stag party. The young men celebrating Michael Harrisonâs incipient wedding to Ashley which is to take place in three days have known each other for years, so whenever one of the friends marries, they plot practical jokes and get blind drunk. Michael himself has been behind several particularly fiendish jokes, so his friends are looking forward to the payback they have developed for Michael. Days before, with shovels and a coffin and a breathing tube, the men prepared the hole in the ground where Michael will be spending the night resting. Because they are not complete idiots, they will leave a flashlight, a porn magazine, a bottle of whisky and a walkie-talkie on his stomach before screwing down the lid and replacing the dirt they had removed for the coffin.<br /><br />As you, gentler reader, may guess, things do not go as planned after they bury the intoxicated Michael and drunkenly drive off. In fact, it all becomes rather horrifying.<br /><br />Grace is a sad 39-year-old man, still mourning for his wife Sandy who mysteriously vanished almost 9 years ago. He is burying himself in his work. Perhaps this predilection is why he eventually gets to the solution of the puzzle of the missing bridegroom. However, Grace cannot bestow salvation on the already damned.<br /><br />What an incredibly exciting and intricate read! It is easy for me to recommend this tricky first book in the Detective Superintendent (we mystery fans immediately know this is a United Kingdom mystery by the rank title) Roy Grace series. I was strongly reminded of an Alfred Hitchcock movie by the plot. There are so many twists and turns a dramamine (emphasize on the <i>drama</i>) might be called for, except the reader will not be putting this book down to sleep, much less eat or go to work.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I have one qualm on recommending âDead Simpleâ. Although the book IS exciting, and <i>I </i>did not guess what the next twist would reveal, by the conclusion more jaded readers might be put off by the authorâs tossing in almost every mystery plot convention made familiar by Hitchcockâs blond dame movies. For me, these familiar surprises did not detract from my enjoyment or my level of expectation. I did not guess correctly what would happen next.<br /><br />Grace utilizes genuine mediums who can truly feel out locations and see clues to a person's circumstances. If, as a mystery reader, you hate genre crossovers or even a hint of a paranormal turn of events, this book will ultimately annoy.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2083362282" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer43813433048215581">Author Peter James had his thirteenth book in the Roy Grace series published earlier this year. Since Iâd never read a book by him before, I apparently felt like that was the right time to start and naturally, I began with book number one because I just canât help myself. Still, the odds that I will have caught up on this series by the time book fourteen comes around are pretty slim and thereâs something quite satisfying in knowing you donât need to anxiously await a publication date.<br/><br/>Dead Simple</span>
  <span id="freeText43813433048215581" style="display:none">Author Peter James had his thirteenth book in the Roy Grace series published earlier this year. Since Iâd never read a book by him before, I apparently felt like that was the right time to start and naturally, I began with book number one because I just canât help myself. Still, the odds that I will have caught up on this series by the time book fourteen comes around are pretty slim and thereâs something quite satisfying in knowing you donât need to anxiously await a publication date.<br /><br />Dead Simple, the first book in the Roy Grace series, is anything but. Itâs complicated, gripping and a fabulous page-turner. Yet it all starts so innocently. Five friends are out on a stag party and the groom-to-be has no idea whatâs in store for him. Itâs meant to be a harmless prank but then the groom-to-be, Michael, goes missing and his friends turn up dead. Enter Detective Superintendent Roy Grace who is sadly all too familiar with missing persons cases as his own wife disappeared without a trace years ago.<br /><br />The story starts off brilliantly and is well-paced throughout. Although it was clear quite early on what was going on, there were still a few twists and turns to keep me absolutely hooked. I found it to be quite an intense ride and a true page-turner as the race against time unfolds to save Michael. This is one of those books where I get incredibly annoyed that my eyes stop cooperating and I have to stop reading because itâs just made to be read in one sitting. This is such a brilliantly executed and completely engrossing plot.<br /><br />I warmed to Roy Grace from the beginning. Heâs incredibly perceptive and determined, willing to do whatever it takes to find out the truth. I love his backstory and am curious to find out if this will be addressed in future.<br /><br />Right off the bat, itâs obvious that Peter James is a fantastic storyteller and itâs easy to see why heâs a bestselling author. I already feel like this may turn out to be one of my favourite series. It seems rather disgraceful that Iâve left it so long in reading one of his books but now I canât wait to get caught up! Highly recommend this one!</span>

<div id="review_1593870689" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1593870689" />
    <a title="L.M. Krier" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50190507-l-m-krier"><img alt="L.M. Krier" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1450343101p2/50190507.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1593870689?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="L.M. Krier" class="user" itemprop="url" name="L.M. Krier" href="/user/show/50190507-l-m-krier">L.M. Krier</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1593870689" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13856635665262782372">This was the first Peter James book I have read. I read it in French from my local library. It came highly recommended by various crime groups on social media. If there was a half-star option, for me it would be a definite 3.5 star.<br/><br/>It starts off well, with a stag night prank which goes horribly wrong. **Only a spoiler if you speak French**. Ironically, in French, a stag night is an enterrement de vie de garÃ§on. It's the stuff of many people's nightmares, although you do need to suspend belief at</span>
  <span id="freeText13856635665262782372" style="display:none">This was the first Peter James book I have read. I read it in French from my local library. It came highly recommended by various crime groups on social media. If there was a half-star option, for me it would be a definite 3.5 star.<br /><br />It starts off well, with a stag night prank which goes horribly wrong. **Only a spoiler if you speak French**. Ironically, in French, a stag night is an enterrement de vie de garÃ§on. It's the stuff of many people's nightmares, although you do need to suspend belief at quite a few points in the narrative.<br /><br />It is certainly a page-turner, in that I continued to read, interested to find out exactly what all the twists and turns would be. One or two were, I found, predictable; one was signalled far too early on for my personal taste.<br /><br />Two things stopped it being a 5-star for me. Although it is well written, mostly with good pace, I found sometimes it dragged, with far more detail than I wanted or needed to know. The poker game, for an example. Okay, I get it, Roy Grace likes to play poker. Fine. I really didn't need to know every bid and every turn of the card. Also, try as I might, I couldn't warm to Grace at all. As a pretty lively sixty-something myself, I found him incredibly dull and middle-aged for a forty-year-old, forty being very much the new thirty. It may well be that's a throw back from when it was written. I still think he comes over as too old for his age.<br /><br />His backstory was interesting, but I wonder if it will ever go anywhere? Perhaps just a hook to make me want to read more of the series. <br /><br />Overall, a good read, but it didn't quite fill me with the enthusiasm I thought it might.</span>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText12441659406592537613" style="display:none">4.5 stars rounded up<br />For my full review of this first book in what promises to be an excellent series, visit my blog:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://fictionophile.wordpress.com/2019/02/28/dead-simple-by-peter-james/">https://fictionophile.wordpress.com/2...</a><br /><br />MY THOUGHTS<br /><br />If you are looking for a British Police Procedural series with an engaging protagonist, then look no further.Â  Roy Grace is one of those coppers that you just can't help but like.<br /><br />The East Sussex setting, during the last week of May, brought the narrative into sharp focus. The characterization was exemplary and the police case interesting and suspenseful. Containing several plot twists, this novel will keep even the most ardent thriller reader happy.<br /><br />"Dead Simple" is a novel that expounds on the lengths some people will go to further their jealousy and greed.Â  It is the first in a series that I plan to pursue with enjoyment.<br /><br />As of now, there are 14 titles in the DS Roy Grace series. It would look as though I have some serious catching up to do!Â  <br /><br />I hope that somewhere in the next thirteen novels I will discover just what happened to Roy Grace's wife Sandy and that we see him getting on with his life.<br /><br />A great and suspense-filled read which makes an excellent start to a series.<br /><br />I received a digital copy of this novel from Hannah Feeney @wunderkindPR for reviewing purposes. All opinions are my own.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12441659406592537613" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText7337396957740838359" style="display:none">DEAD SIMPLE (Police Procedural-UK-Cont) â VG<br />James, Peter â 1st of series<br />Macmillan, 2005 â UK Hardcover<br />Detective Superintendent Roy Graceâs wife disappeared several years ago without a trace. Now Grace is asked by Ashley Harper to find her fiancÃ©e, missing three days before their wedding. Michael Harrison is a practical joker. But his friends have turned the table, taken him out, got him drunk and buried him in a coffin with an air tube. Jamesâ previous books look to be more in the horror or psychological suspense category, where this is a solid police procedural. <span id="freeTextContainer12488898908448450398">I was lucky enough to be able to read an ARC of the authors latest book The House On Cold Hill which I loved. I hadn't actually read anything else by the author even though I had already bought Dead Simple a while back but just not got round to reading it. Well after reading The House On Cold Hill I had to bump Dead Simple up my reading pile and boy am I glad I did. <br/><br/>Wow oh wow oh wow! That is how I felt when I finished this novel. The adrenalin is still coursing through me now whilst writing thi</span>
  <span id="freeText12488898908448450398" style="display:none">I was lucky enough to be able to read an ARC of the authors latest book The House On Cold Hill which I loved. I hadn't actually read anything else by the author even though I had already bought Dead Simple a while back but just not got round to reading it. Well after reading The House On Cold Hill I had to bump Dead Simple up my reading pile and boy am I glad I did. <br /><br />Wow oh wow oh wow! That is how I felt when I finished this novel. The adrenalin is still coursing through me now whilst writing this review. I honestly feel like I have just got off one of the best roller coaster rides of my life.<br /><br />Dead Simple starts off brilliantly and just does not stop. This really is a story of a race against time and the reader very much feels the pressure that Detective Superintendent Grace is under to try and find missing groom to be, Michael.<br /><br />It is really hard to say to much about this story with out giving to much away. I do have to say what happens to Michael at the beginning of the story is most peoples worst nightmare but what is even worse is that things get even worse for him which I would never have thought possible.<br /><br />Dead Simple is a non stop, fast paced read which by the end I could not get through the pages quick enough to see how things were going to end. Be prepared from picking up this book to not being able to put it back down until you have read it, that's how good it is. <br /><br />The best bit about this books is that it is the first in the series of books following Detective Superintendent Grace so I am over the moon that I have lots more books to look forward to reading by Peter James who I am now becoming a huge fan of.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5773998090868138343">The beginning of this story was so uncomfortably tense that I almost didn't carry on reading but I am so glad I did otherwise I would have missed a smashing tale. <br/>The mystery unfolds layer by layer, by twists and turns, piling on more tension and urgency all the way. At first I considered some of the twists came a little fortuitously out of the blue. Sometimes I can be a bit thick. It soon sank in that it was exactly how it would have appeared to the two main tellers of the tale. Thank heavens M</span>
  <span id="freeText5773998090868138343" style="display:none">The beginning of this story was so uncomfortably tense that I almost didn't carry on reading but I am so glad I did otherwise I would have missed a smashing tale. <br />The mystery unfolds layer by layer, by twists and turns, piling on more tension and urgency all the way. At first I considered some of the twists came a little fortuitously out of the blue. Sometimes I can be a bit thick. It soon sank in that it was exactly how it would have appeared to the two main tellers of the tale. Thank heavens Mr James, the author, is a bit cleverer than I am. There are distractions, several red herrings and at least one reveal that stopped me in my tracks. I warmed to the police characters, even the smallest bit player is deftly defined and rounded out. DS Grace is intriguing. He is gentle but astute and foccussed in his investigations. I found his attitude to the paranormal totally believable. This side of the story does not overwhelm the mystery. He is not evangelistic about using psychics, in fact he learns a lesson early on in this story about the wisdom of keeping quiet about it. The medium and diviner are just part of this detective's tool box. <br />I am looking forward very much to reading more about the world of Roy Grace.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5773998090868138343" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5466291821383430381">I've come to the conclusion I'm not a fan of Peter James and that it's now finally over between us, I've read four or five of his and have yet to be wowed. This was for me, only OK, I got a slight kick out of it as it's set in Brighton, I live there so I enjoyed the familiarity of the locations. The chapters from inside the coffin were well written and tense but the characters all felt very flat to me. I have to have either an absolutely ripping yarn or brilliant characters and if there's both I</span>
  <span id="freeText5466291821383430381" style="display:none">I've come to the conclusion I'm not a fan of Peter James and that it's now finally over between us, I've read four or five of his and have yet to be wowed. This was for me, only OK, I got a slight kick out of it as it's set in Brighton, I live there so I enjoyed the familiarity of the locations. The chapters from inside the coffin were well written and tense but the characters all felt very flat to me. I have to have either an absolutely ripping yarn or brilliant characters and if there's both I'm as happy as a pig in poop, unfortunately this one didn't deliver enough on any level. Ta-ra Peter.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5466291821383430381" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2718832257" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2718832257" />
    <a title="Jenny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12227138-jenny"><img alt="Jenny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578130339p2/12227138.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2718832257?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenny" href="/user/show/12227138-jenny">Jenny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/44033568-dead-simple">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12227138-jenny?shelf=england">england</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12227138-jenny?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12227138-jenny?shelf=crime">crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2718832257" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11840175039617801860">Dead Simple is book one in the Roy Grace series by Peter James. Four mates Robbo, Luke, Michael and Josh, went out for the evening to celebrate Michael last night as a single man before his wedding to Ashley. Robbo Luke and Josh decide to give Michael a night to remember and buried him in with a breathing tube and a phone. However, Rob, Luke and Josh well-planed prank was derailed when they were involved in a road accident. Detective Superintendent Roy Grace became involved when Ashley reported </span>
  <span id="freeText11840175039617801860" style="display:none">Dead Simple is book one in the Roy Grace series by Peter James. Four mates Robbo, Luke, Michael and Josh, went out for the evening to celebrate Michael last night as a single man before his wedding to Ashley. Robbo Luke and Josh decide to give Michael a night to remember and buried him in with a breathing tube and a phone. However, Rob, Luke and Josh well-planed prank was derailed when they were involved in a road accident. Detective Superintendent Roy Grace became involved when Ashley reported Michael missing. The readers of Dead Simple will continue to follow the twist and turns in Detective Superintendent Roy Grace investigation into the disappearance of Michael. Also, the readers of Dead Simple will be surprised by the conclusion of this book. <br /><br />I read the later books in this series, and I please that I am going back to the beginning because you learn more about the characters and how the author's first thoughts about the main characters. Dead Simple is well written and researched by Peter James. I love Peter James portrayal of his characters and the way they interact with each other. The like the way Peter James describes his settings that allow me to engage with the story and the characters.<br /><br />The readers of Dead Simple will learn about the grieve that people suffer when loved ones go missing. Also, the readers of Dead Simple will learn about the devastation that greed, revenge and jealousy have on people. <br /><br />I recommend this book</span>
  <a data-text-id="11840175039617801860" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('D05Yt+qxOwDk6AOvkoIItQsvKt0c1lrZe7wvlu+u1ox+KIVTOt1PH2DvekM3w9vB0wxqlHsP6cjGTSXbN8pcNg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('eigS3AXHXhtabsysd0Injv8CwUomt/60LtvCaQFSyb0LTs841asqBN5ptUDSA/T6JyGBA0FuTaWTKsgk2TZDBw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

  <span id="freeText9094049911556765160" style="display:none">Peter James is a global bestselling author, best known for writing crime and thriller novels, and the creator of the much-loved Detective Superintendent Roy Grace. With a total of 16 Sunday Times No. 1s under his belt, he has achieved global book sales of over 20 million copies to date and has been translated into 37 languages.<br /><br />Synonymous with plot-twisting page-turners, Peter has garnered an army of loyal fans throughout his storytelling career â which also included stints writing for TV and producing films. He has won over 40 awards for his work, including the WHSmith Best Crime Author of All Time Award, Crime Writersâ Association Diamond Dagger and a BAFTA nomination for The Merchant of Venice starring Al Pacino and Jeremy Irons for which he was an Executive Producer. Many of Peterâs novels have been adapted for film, TV and stage.</span>
